Buenos Aires [bid](/wiki/Buenos_Aires_bid_for_the_2018_Summer_Youth_Olympics "Buenos Aires bid for the 2018 Summer Youth Olympics") to host the [2018 Summer Youth Olympics](/wiki/2018_Summer_Youth_Olympics "2018 Summer Youth Olympics").^[\[237\]](#cite_note-241)^ On 4 July 2013, the IOC elected Buenos Aires as the host city.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-autogenerated1-242)^ Buenos Aires hosted the [2006 South American Games](/wiki/2006_South_American_Games "2006 South American Games") too.{#cite_ref-autogenerated1_242-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/La_Bombonera.jpg/220px-La_Bombonera.jpg)](/wiki/File:La_Bombonera.jpg) *[La Bombonera](/wiki/La_Bombonera "La Bombonera")* during a night game of [Copa Libertadores](/wiki/Copa_Libertadores "Copa Libertadores") between [Boca Juniors](/wiki/Boca_Juniors "Boca Juniors") v. [Colo Colo](/wiki/Colo_Colo "Colo Colo")

[Football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") is a popular pastime among many of the city's citizens, as Buenos Aires, featuring no fewer than 24 professional teams, has the highest concentration of teams of any city in the world.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-observer-243)^ with many of its teams playing in the major league. The [best-known rivalry](/wiki/Supercl%C3%A1sico "Superclásico") is the one between [Boca Juniors](/wiki/Boca_Juniors "Boca Juniors") and [River Plate](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_River_Plate "Club Atlético River Plate"), the match is better known as [Superclásico](/wiki/Supercl%C3%A1sico "Superclásico"). Watching a match between these two teams was deemed one of the "50 sporting things you must do before you die" by *The Observer* .^[\[239\]](#cite_note-observer-243)^ Other major clubs include [San Lorenzo de Almagro](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_San_Lorenzo_de_Almagro "Club Atlético San Lorenzo de Almagro"), [Club Atlético Huracán](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Hurac%C3%A1n "Club Atlético Huracán"), [Vélez Sarsfield](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_V%C3%A9lez_Sarsfield "Club Atlético Vélez Sarsfield"), [Chacarita Juniors](/wiki/Chacarita_Juniors "Chacarita Juniors"), [Club Ferro Carril Oeste](/wiki/Club_Ferro_Carril_Oeste "Club Ferro Carril Oeste"), [Nueva Chicago](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Nueva_Chicago "Club Atlético Nueva Chicago") and [Asociación Atlética Argentinos Juniors](/wiki/Asociaci%C3%B3n_Atl%C3%A9tica_Argentinos_Juniors "Asociación Atlética Argentinos Juniors"). [Diego Maradona](/wiki/Diego_Maradona "Diego Maradona"), born in [Lanús Partido](/wiki/Lan%C3%BAs_Partido "Lanús Partido"), a county south of Buenos Aires, is widely hailed as one of the sport's greatest players of all time. Maradona started his career with [Argentinos Juniors](/wiki/Argentinos_Juniors "Argentinos Juniors") and went on to play for [Boca Juniors](/wiki/Boca_Juniors "Boca Juniors"), the [national football team](/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team "Argentina national football team") and others (most notably [FC Barcelona](/wiki/FC_Barcelona "FC Barcelona") in Spain and [SSC Napoli](/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli "S.S.C. Napoli") in Italy).^[\[240\]](#cite_note-244)^{#cite_ref-244}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/La_Catedral_del_Polo.jpg/220px-La_Catedral_del_Polo.jpg)](/wiki/File:La_Catedral_del_Polo.jpg) [Campo Argentino de Polo](/wiki/Campo_Argentino_de_Polo "Campo Argentino de Polo"), home of the [Argentine Open Polo Championship](/wiki/Argentine_Open_Polo_Championship "Argentine Open Polo Championship"), the most important global event of this discipline [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Court_central_Buenos_Aires_Lawn_Tennis_Club.jpg/220px-Court_central_Buenos_Aires_Lawn_Tennis_Club.jpg)](/wiki/File:Court_central_Buenos_Aires_Lawn_Tennis_Club.jpg) [Buenos Aires Lawn Tennis Club](/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Lawn_Tennis_Club "Buenos Aires Lawn Tennis Club")

In 1912, the practice of basketball in Argentina was started by the *Asociación Cristiana de Jóvenes (YMCA)* of Buenos Aires,^[\[241\]](#cite_note-245)^ when Canadian professor Paul Phillip was in charge of teaching basketball at the YMCA of Paseo Colón Avenue. The first basketball clubs in Argentina, [Hindú](/wiki/Hind%C3%BA_Club "Hindú Club") and [Independiente](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Independiente "Club Atlético Independiente"), were located at the YMCAs of the [Greater Buenos Aires](/wiki/Greater_Buenos_Aires "Greater Buenos Aires") metropolitan area. By 1912 the first basketball games were held by YMCA headquarters in Buenos Aires. Nowadays, the [Argentine Basketball Confederation](/wiki/Argentine_Basketball_Confederation "Argentine Basketball Confederation") is headquartered in Buenos Aires.{#cite_ref-245}

Argentina has been the home of world champions in professional [boxing](/wiki/Boxing "Boxing"). [Carlos Monzon](/wiki/Carlos_Monzon "Carlos Monzon") was a hall of fame World Middleweight champion, and the former lineal Middleweight champion [Sergio Martinez](/wiki/Sergio_Mart%C3%ADnez_(boxer) "Sergio Martínez (boxer)") hails from Argentina. [Omar Narvaez](/wiki/Omar_Narv%C3%A1ez_(boxer) "Omar Narváez (boxer)"), [Lucas Matthysse](/wiki/Lucas_Matthysse "Lucas Matthysse"), [Carolina Duer](/wiki/Carolina_Duer "Carolina Duer"), and [Marcos Maidana](/wiki/Marcos_Maidana "Marcos Maidana") are five modern-day world champions as well.

Argentines' love for horses can be experienced in several ways: [horse racing](/wiki/Horse_racing "Horse racing") at the *[Hipódromo Argentino de Palermo](/wiki/Hip%C3%B3dromo_Argentino_de_Palermo "Hipódromo Argentino de Palermo")* [racetrack](/wiki/Race_track "Race track"), [polo](/wiki/Polo "Polo") in the *[Campo Argentino de Polo](/wiki/Campo_Argentino_de_Polo "Campo Argentino de Polo")* (located just across Libertador Avenue from the *Hipódromo* ), and [pato](/wiki/Pato "Pato"), a kind of basketball played on horseback that was declared the national game in 1953. Polo was brought to the country in the second half of the 19th century by English immigrants.

The first rugby union match in Argentina was played in 1873 in the [Buenos Aires Cricket Club Ground](/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Cricket_Club_Ground "Buenos Aires Cricket Club Ground"), located in the neighborhood of [Palermo](/wiki/Palermo,_Buenos_Aires "Palermo, Buenos Aires"), where the [Galileo Galilei planetarium](/wiki/Galileo_Galilei_planetarium "Galileo Galilei planetarium") is located today. Rugby enjoys widespread popularity in Buenos Aires, most especially in the north of the city, which boasts more than eighty rugby clubs. The city is home to the Argentine [Super Rugby](/wiki/Super_Rugby "Super Rugby") franchise, the [Jaguares](/wiki/Jaguares_(Super_Rugby) "Jaguares (Super Rugby)"). The [Argentina national rugby union team](/wiki/Argentina_national_rugby_union_team "Argentina national rugby union team") competes in Buenos Aires in international matches such as the [Rugby Championship](/wiki/The_Rugby_Championship "The Rugby Championship").

Buenos Aires native [Guillermo Vilas](/wiki/Guillermo_Vilas "Guillermo Vilas") (who was raised in [Mar del Plata](/wiki/Mar_del_Plata "Mar del Plata")) and [Gabriela Sabatini](/wiki/Gabriela_Sabatini "Gabriela Sabatini") were great tennis players of the 1970s and 1980s^[\[182\]](#cite_note-Time_Out-186)^ and popularized tennis Nationwide in Argentina. Vilas won the [ATP Buenos Aires](/wiki/ATP_Buenos_Aires "ATP Buenos Aires") numerous times in the 1970s. Other popular sports in Buenos Aires are [golf](/wiki/Golf "Golf"), [basketball](/wiki/Basketball "Basketball"), [rugby](/wiki/Rugby_union "Rugby union") and [field hockey](/wiki/Field_hockey "Field hockey").{#cite_ref-Time_Out_186-3}

[Juan Manuel Fangio](/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Fangio "Juan Manuel Fangio") won five [Formula One World Driver's Championships](/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Drivers%27_Champions "List of Formula One World Drivers' Champions"), and was only outstripped by [Michael Schumacher](/wiki/Michael_Schumacher "Michael Schumacher") and [Lewis Hamilton](/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton "Lewis Hamilton"), with seven Championships. The Buenos Aires [Oscar Gálvez](/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Juan_y_Oscar_G%C3%A1lvez "Autódromo Juan y Oscar Gálvez") car-racing track hosted 20 [Formula One](/wiki/Formula_One "Formula One") events as the [Argentine Grand Prix](/wiki/Argentine_Grand_Prix "Argentine Grand Prix"), between 1953 and 1998; it was discontinued on financial grounds. The track features various local categories on most weekends. The [2009](/wiki/2009_Dakar_Rally "2009 Dakar Rally"), [2010](/wiki/2010_Dakar_Rally "2010 Dakar Rally"), [2011](/wiki/2011_Dakar_Rally "2011 Dakar Rally"), [2015](/wiki/2015_Dakar_Rally "2015 Dakar Rally") Dakar Rally started and ended in the city.  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/River_Monumental_Panoramic.jpg/1000px-River_Monumental_Panoramic.jpg)](/wiki/File:River_Monumental_Panoramic.jpg "El Monumental, home of River Plate, hosted the final game of the FIFA World Cup Championship in 1978.")  
[](/wiki/File:River_Monumental_Panoramic.jpg "File:River Monumental Panoramic.jpg")
[*El Monumental*](/wiki/Estadio_Monumental_Antonio_Vespucio_Liberti "Estadio Monumental Antonio Vespucio Liberti"), home of [River Plate](/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_River_Plate "Club Atlético River Plate"), hosted the final game of the [FIFA World Cup Championship in 1978](/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup "1978 FIFA World Cup").

Buenos Aires held the [1st FIBA World Championship in 1950](/wiki/1950_FIBA_World_Championship "1950 FIBA World Championship") and [11th FIBA World Championship in 1990](/wiki/1990_FIBA_World_Championship "1990 FIBA World Championship"), the [1st Pan American Games in 1951](/wiki/1951_Pan_American_Games "1951 Pan American Games"), was the site of two venues in the [1978 FIFA World Cup](/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup "1978 FIFA World Cup") and one in the [1982 FIVB Men's World Championship](/wiki/1982_FIVB_Men%27s_World_Championship "1982 FIVB Men's World Championship"). Most recently, Buenos Aires had a venue in the [2001 FIFA World Youth Championship](/wiki/2001_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship "2001 FIFA World Youth Championship") and in the [2002 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship](/wiki/2002_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship "2002 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship"), hosted the [125th IOC Session](/wiki/125th_IOC_Session "125th IOC Session") in 2013, the [2018 Summer Youth Olympics](/wiki/2018_Summer_Youth_Olympics "2018 Summer Youth Olympics")^[\[238\]](#cite_note-autogenerated1-242)^ and the [2018 G20 summit](/wiki/2018_G20_Buenos_Aires_summit "2018 G20 Buenos Aires summit").^[\[242\]](#cite_note-246)^{#cite_ref-246}  

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

### Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities {#Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Buenos_Aires&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities")\]

Buenos Aires is part of the [Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities](/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities "Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities")^[\[270\]](#cite_note-274)^ from 12 October 1982 establishing brotherly relations with the following cities:{#cite_ref-274}  
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/22px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png) [Andorra la Vella](/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella "Andorra la Vella"), Andorra
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Paraguay.svg/23px-Flag_of_Paraguay.svg.png) [Asunción](/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n "Asunción"), Paraguay
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png) [Bogotá](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1 "Bogotá"), Colombia
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/23px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png) [Caracas](/wiki/Caracas "Caracas"), Venezuela
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Flag_of_Guatemala.svg/23px-Flag_of_Guatemala.svg.png) [Guatemala City](/wiki/Guatemala_City "Guatemala City"), Guatemala
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png) [Havana](/wiki/Havana "Havana"), Cuba
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/22px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png) [La Paz](/wiki/La_Paz "La Paz"), Bolivia
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/23px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png) [Lima](/wiki/Lima "Lima"), Peru
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png) [Lisbon](/wiki/Lisbon "Lisbon"), Portugal
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png) [Madrid](/wiki/Madrid "Madrid"), Spain
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png) [Managua](/wiki/Managua "Managua"), Nicaragua
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png) [Mexico City](/wiki/Mexico_City "Mexico City"), Mexico
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Uruguay.svg/23px-Flag_of_Uruguay.svg.png) [Montevideo](/wiki/Montevideo "Montevideo"), Uruguay
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Flag_of_Panama.svg/23px-Flag_of_Panama.svg.png) [Panama City](/wiki/Panama_City "Panama City"), Panama
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flag_of_Ecuador.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ecuador.svg.png) [Quito](/wiki/Quito "Quito"), Ecuador
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png) [Rio de Janeiro](/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro "Rio de Janeiro"), Brazil
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg/23px-Flag_of_Costa_Rica.svg.png) [San José](/wiki/San_Jose_(Costa_Rica) "San Jose (Costa Rica)"), Costa Rica
* ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Puerto_Rico.svg.png) [San Juan](/wiki/San_Juan_(Puerto_Rico) "San Juan (Puerto Rico)"), Puerto Rico, United States

Notes {#Notes}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Buenos_Aires&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Notes")\]  
1. **[\^](#cite_ref-5)** Buenos Aires was founded twice, first on 2 February 1536; 489 years ago (1536-02-02) by [Pedro de Mendoza](/wiki/Pedro_de_Mendoza "Pedro de Mendoza").{#cite_note-5}
{#cite_note-5}
2. **[\^](#cite_ref-7)** [Greater Buenos Aires](/wiki/Greater_Buenos_Aires "Greater Buenos Aires") -- Autonomous City and 24 districts ([partidos](/wiki/Partidos_of_Buenos_Aires "Partidos of Buenos Aires")){#cite_note-7}
{#cite_note-7}
3. **[\^](#cite_ref-9)** According to [INDEC](/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_and_Census_of_Argentina "National Institute of Statistics and Census of Argentina"), the Metropolitan Region of Buenos Aires has Autonomous City and 39 districts (partidos):^[\[6\]](#cite_note-Indec.Census(2022)-8)^ *Almirante Brown, Avellaneda, Berazategui, Berisso, Brandsen, Campana, Cañuelas, Ensenada, Escobar, Esteban Echeverría, Exaltación de la Cruz, Ezeiza, Florencio Varela, General Rodríguez, General San Martín, Hurlingham, Ituzaingó, José C. Paz, La Matanza, Lanús, La Plata, Lomas de Zamora, Luján, Malvinas Argentinas, Marcos Paz, Merlo, Moreno, Morón, Pilar, Presidente Perón, Quilmes, San Fernando, San Isidro, San Miguel, San Vicente, Tigre, Tres de Febrero, Vicente López y Zárate.*{#cite_ref-Indec.Census(2022)_8-0}
{#cite_note-9}
4. **[\^](#cite_ref-17)** Spanish: *Ciudad Autónoma de Buenos Aires*{#cite_note-17}
{#cite_note-17}

### Further reading {#Further_reading}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Buenos_Aires&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Further reading")\]  
Further information: [Bibliography of the history of Buenos Aires](/wiki/Timeline_of_Buenos_Aires#Bibliography "Timeline of Buenos Aires")  
* Adelman, Jeremy. *Republic of capital: Buenos Aires and the legal transformation of the Atlantic world* (Stanford University Press, 1999)
* Baily, Samuel L. "The Adjustment of Italian Immigrants in Buenos Aires and New York, 1870--1914." *American Historical Review* (1983): 281--305. [in JSTOR](https://www.jstor.org/stable/1865403) [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20160311125727/http://www.jstor.org/stable/1865403) 11 March 2016 at the [Wayback Machine](/wiki/Wayback_Machine "Wayback Machine")
* Bao, Sandra, and Bridget Gleeson. *Lonely Planet Buenos Aires* (Travel Guide) (2011)
* Benson, Andrew. *The Rough Guide to Buenos Aires* (2011)
* *Buenos Aires Travel Guide 2014: Essential Tourist Information, Maps \& Photos* (2014)
* Emerson, Charles. *1913: In Search of the World Before the Great War* (2013) compares Buenos Aires to 20 major world cities; pp 252--66.
* Keeling, David J. *Buenos Aires: Global dreams, local crises* (Wiley, 1996)
* Moya, Jose C. *Cousins and strangers: Spanish immigrants in Buenos Aires, 1850--1930* (University of California Press, 1998)
* Mulhall, Michael George, and Edward T. Mulhall. *Handbook of the River Plate: Comprising Buenos Ayres, the Upper Provinces, Banda Oriental, Paraguay* (2 vol. 1869) [online](https://books.google.com/books?id=wOCEAAAAIAAJ) [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20240226125235/https://books.google.com/books?lr=lang_en&id=wOCEAAAAIAAJ) 26 February 2024 at the [Wayback Machine](/wiki/Wayback_Machine "Wayback Machine")
* Scobie, James R. *Buenos Aires: plaza to suburb, 1870--1910* (Oxford University Press, 1974)
* Socolow, Susan Migden. *The Merchants of Buenos Aires, 1778--1810: Family and Commerce* (Cambridge University Press, 1978)
* Sofer, Eugene F. *From Pale to Pampa: A social history of the Jews of Buenos Aires* (Holmes \& Meier, 1982)
